# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

## Your Task

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossrepo tracing domain.

## Available Resources

92-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the complete TLS configuration flow from Prometheus through prometheus-common. Here's a summary of what I found:

## TLS Configuration Chain Overview

The TLS configuration flows through the following key components:

### **prometheus-common (Core TLS Handling)**
- **TLSConfig struct**: Stores CA file, cert file, key file, server name, and insecure skip verify settings
- **NewTLSConfig()**: Converts the config struct to Go's `*tls.Config` by loading certificates and CA files
- **HTTPClientConfig struct**: Wraps TLSConfig along with auth settings
- **NewClientFromConfig()**: Creates HTTP clients from configuration
- **NewRoundTripperFromConfig()**: Creates HTTP RoundTripper with TLS support

### **prometheus Config Layer**
Four main configuration structures use TLS:
1. **ScrapeConfig** - for scraping metrics from targets
2. **RemoteWriteConfig** - for writing to remote storage
3. **RemoteReadConfig** - for reading from remote storage
4. **TracingConfig** - for OTLP tracing endpoints

### **Application Points**
- **Scrape targets**: `scrape/scrape.go::newScrapeClient()` → calls NewClientFromConfig
- **Remote write**: `storage/remote/client.go::NewWriteClient()` → calls NewClientFromConfig
- **Remote read**: `storage/remote/client.go::NewReadClient()` → calls NewClientFromConfig
- **Tracing (OTLP)**: `tracing/tracing.go::getClient()` → calls NewTLSConfig for both gRPC and HTTP clients

The complete answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all relevant files, symbols, and a detailed explanation of the TLS configuration flow.

server certificate verification\\n   - CertFile: path to client certificate file\\n   - KeyFile: path to client private key file\\n   - ServerName: for hostname verification\\n   - InsecureSkipVerify: flag to skip certificate verification\\n\\n2. **NewTLSConfig function** (lines 293-325): Converts TLSConfig struct to Go's *tls.Config by:\\n   - Creating a tls.Config with InsecureSkipVerify setting\\n   - Loading and parsing CA certificates from CAFile\\n   - Setting ServerName for TLS handshake\\n   - Loading client certificates and setting GetClientCertificate callback\\n   - Handling file validation and error cases\\n\\n3. **HTTPClientConfig struct** (lines 75-86): Wraps TLSConfig along with:\\n   - BasicAuth credentials\\n   - BearerToken authentication\\n   - Proxy URL settings\\n   - TLSConfig field for TLS-specific settings\\n\\n4. **NewClientFromConfig function** (lines 125-131): Creates HTTP client by calling NewRoundTripperFromConfig\\n\\n5. **NewRoundTripperFromConfig function** (lines 135-183): Creates HTTP RoundTripper that:\\n   - Calls NewTLSConfig to convert the TLSConfig struct to *tls.Config\\n   - Passes the tlsConfig to http.Transport's TLSClientConfig field\\n   - Wraps with authentication layers (bearer token, basic auth)\\n   - Creates tlsRoundTripper for automatic CA file reloading if CAFile is specified\\n\\n## Configuration Structures (prometheus)\\n\\nIn `github.com/prometheus/prometheus/config/config.go`:\\n\\n1. **ScrapeConfig struct** (line 830): Contains HTTPClientConfig field (inline) - used for scrape target configuration\\n2. **RemoteWriteConfig struct** (line 1434): Contains HTTPClientConfig field (inline) - used for remote write endpoints\\n3. **RemoteReadConfig struct** (line 1597): Contains HTTPClientConfig field (inline) - used for remote read endpoints\\n4. **TracingConfig struct** (line 1165): Contains TLSConfig field directly - used for OTLP tracing endpoints\\n\\n## Application Points\\n\\n### Scrape Targets\\n\\nIn `github.com/prometheus/prometheus/scrape/scrape.go`:\\n- **newScrapeClient function** (line 2260): Calls `config_util.NewClientFromConfig(cfg, name, `github.com/prometheus/prometheus/storage/remote/client.go`:\\n- **ClientConfig struct** (lines 128-141): Contains HTTPClientConfig field\\n- **NewReadClient function** (line 152): Calls Calls `config_util.NewClientFromConfig(conf.HTTPClientConfig, \\\"remote_storage_write_client\\\", httpOpts...)` to create HTTP client for remote write requests\\n\\n### Tracing (OTLP)\\n\\nIn `github.com/prometheus/prometheus/tracing/tracing.go`:\\n- **buildTracerProvider function** (line 131): Calls getClient with TracingConfig\\n- **getClient function** (line 179): Handles both gRPC and HTTP OTLP clients:\\n  - For gRPC (line 189): Calls `config_util.NewTLSConfig(&tracingCfg.TLSConfig)` and passes result to `otlptracegrpc.WithTLSCredentials(credentials.NewTLS(tlsConf))`\\n  - For HTTP (line 222): Calls `config_util.NewTLSConfig(&tracingCfg.TLSConfig)` and passes result to `otlptracehttp.WithTLSClientConfig(tlsConf)`\\n\\n## Complete Flow\\n\\nThe TLS configuration flow is:\\n1. YAML configuration is parsed into ScrapeConfig, RemoteWriteConfig, RemoteReadConfig, or TracingConfig structs\\n2. Each contains HTTPClientConfig or TLSConfig field with file paths and TLS settings\\n3. When creating HTTP clients:\\n   - prometheus calls config_util.NewClientFromConfig or config_util.NewTLSConfig\\n   - This converts the config struct to *tls.Config by loading certificates and CA files\\n   - The *tls.Config is set in http.Transport's TLSClientConfig field\\n   - The http.Client uses this transport for all HTTPS connections (scrape targets, remote write/read, tracing)\\n4. For scrape and remote storage: HTTPClientConfig flows through NewClientFromConfig \u2192 NewRoundTripperFromConfig \u2192 NewTLSConfig\\n5.
